Professional Exploration

Settling in One's Profession and Finding Joy in One's Work 290

— Xuefei

Nowadays, some people advise people to settle in their professions and find joy in their work. Settling in one's profession means that after getting a job, one should settle down and do the existing job with peace of mind, without being fickle. Finding joy in one's work means that after getting a job, one should develop an interest in the existing job, and not just casually pass the day as it comes, or develop disgust. This is said to those who are generally dissatisfied with the status quo. Under the current situation, it is already difficult for ordinary people to get a job. Having a job, whether it is good or bad, is already extremely fortunate. To be unsettled and not find joy in one's work would be tantamount to seeking one's own death. This is of course unacceptable. Therefore, the topic of "settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work" is even more powerful now.

However, the problem now is not in "settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work," but in the fact that there is no profession that can be settled in, and no profession that can be found joy in. Settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work, the prerequisite is that the profession can at least be settled in and can be found joy in, that is to say, engaging in this profession must at least be able to maintain one's livelihood, and at least be able to use one's spare time to develop one's talent, and then strive to improve and find ways to increase one's knowledge, skills, and abilities to develop this profession. In this way, one can settle in and find joy in this profession. But can it be done now? In fact, it is absolutely impossible. We see that many people work hard all day long, but as a result, they still cannot maintain their family's livelihood, or even their own personal livelihood; they still cannot help but be in debt. In this way, can they settle in this profession? This is one. It's fine to have a job, but unfortunately, in this society, things change unexpectedly from morning to night. Any career is in danger of bankruptcy and destruction at any time; also, the boss's joy and anger can also shake the job at any time. In this way, the job is always in an unstable state. People are only preoccupied with maintaining their position day and night, how can they settle in their profession? This is two. Secondly, most of the current jobs are like those of cattle and horses, that is, you have to devote all your energy to your duties every day, so that you can barely earn enough to be half full. Otherwise, standing behind the boss are people looking for jobs, and he can easily replace you and find someone else who is willing to sell more labor. In this way, you will have no remaining time to use for self-study. You can forget about improving your knowledge and skills, and the future is always empty and distant. Also, what you have learned is not what you are using. In order to eat, you have to take up a profession that you are not interested in, and there are many of these. In this situation, how can you ask them to find joy in their work? Since the prerequisites for settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work are not met, the effects of settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work are of course impossible to achieve.

Therefore, the problem now is not in settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work, but in how one can settle in one's profession and how one can find joy in one's work. If these prerequisites cannot be resolved, then all talk of settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work is empty.

Then, how can we solve these prerequisites for settling in one's profession and finding joy in one's work? This is a big question.

Also, people generally ask people to be diligent, thrifty, and hardworking, which is of course the best thing to do, but unfortunately, this is also empty. It is as difficult as ascending to heaven to find a job now, and it is still as difficult as ascending to heaven to barely maintain a livelihood with it. In this situation, diligence, thrift, and hard work are of course out of the question.

Those without jobs have to find jobs, and those with jobs cannot settle in their professions and find joy in their work. Where should we go? This chaotic society!

Of Speech

Zhang Yousan's Lecture on "The Path to Youth Self-Cultivation" 291

— Shen Pin Records

(A) Understanding oneself: We must recognize our shortcomings and strengths, and reform our shortcomings while developing our strengths. During adolescence, all parts of the body are developed and mature, which is the time for a person to work hard and strive to achieve something. At this time, there are three characteristics in the mental aspect: one is impulsive behavior. During adolescence, there is always a force urging him to act, because in childhood, the strength, knowledge, and body are not enough to act. In old age, because he has been deeply involved in the world and has rich experience, he has to consider the interests of all parties, so he moves less. Second, altruism: his impulsive behavior is altruistic, not selfish. Third, rich social interaction: he is not only altruistic, but also wants to interact with people more and more. However, impulse is short-lived and scattered. We should train it to become a lasting and organized legitimate action. Altruism should cultivate the spirit of being eager to do public good. Social interaction should be trained to be able to cooperate with people, and a complete outlook on life must be understood.

(B) Understanding the nation: Now you can often hear a fashionable saying: "Promote the national spirit," but the Chinese national spirit has good and bad aspects. Now, let's cite the observation points of three famous people from China and abroad to represent the Chinese national spirit. Liang Rengong said that the characteristics of the Chinese national spirit are six: one is slavery, two is ignorance, three is fondness for hypocrisy, four is selfishness, five is sloppiness, and six is fondness for profit. Japanese Ōsaka Shūsai said there are eight: one is belief in fate, two is loyalty and filial piety, three is weakness, four is fondness for profit, five is selfishness, six is conservatism, seven is interesting, and eight is contradictions. The American Huntington said there are seven: one is lack of organizational skills, two is selfishness, three is diligence and hard work, four is laziness, five is hypocrisy, six is loyalty and filial piety, and seven is conservatism. Combining the observations of the three, the Chinese nation has two major shortcomings: one is selfishness, and two is fondness for conservatism and lack of ambition. Japanese Araki Sadao said to the League of Nations investigation team; Chinese people are like sand, they cannot be combined together, and Japanese people are like cement, they have solidarity. When Japanese people mention Greater Japan, they have an incredible spirit. Recently, a famous educator actually said: "It's better to do less than to do more." This spirit of muddling along is the most common characteristic of China. Speaking of foreigners saying that Chinese people love peace, this kind of peace is used to deal with foreigners. Once the soldiers are under the city, they talk about peace. As for their own people in the country? Just look at the public buses in Shanghai driving on the road. If the rickshaw in front is a little slow, there will be a pig-like shout. If the rickshaw puller replies to him, he may come down and fight him. This situation can be seen everywhere in China. Also, the best spirit of the Chinese, hard work and endurance, is now slowly degenerating, so we must cultivate the national spirit that the Chinese nation needs.

(C) Understanding the times: We should (1) pay attention to true thoughts (that is, the spirit and method of science), observe with an objective attitude, and abandon subjective and mysterious thoughts. (2) Pay attention to the welfare of the masses. There is an ancient Greek saying: "Man is the measure of all things." Now let us add a sentence, that is, this person must seek the welfare of the masses and the nation.

Shang Tang has a saying: "If you can one day renovate yourself, do so again and again, and forever renovate yourself," this spirit of continuous self-improvement can be used as a model for us. Now all countries in the world advocate "survival of the fittest." The term competition is both progressive and harmful to the same kind. It is completely a selfish behavior, that is, the strong prey on the weak. We should advocate cooperation, "I am for everyone, and everyone is for me." Cooperation is the most modern, the most perfect, and the most universal self-cultivation.

In short, the purpose of self-cultivation is to cultivate a socialized personality. The welfare of society is my welfare. There is no small self, only a big self. Integrating society and myself, self-cultivation is for the sake of society. Goethe said it well: "A good character is never cultivated in selfish ideas." We must fundamentally eradicate the root of the disease and observe ourselves with an objective attitude. Lu Xun said: "To develop an objective attitude, you must be interested in all aspects of the business." For example, in a speech, don't always pay attention to your own posture, movements, and attitude. You must devote all your energy to paying attention to the audience and forget yourself. To cultivate a great personality, you must work hard for mankind and for society, and you must not have the hope of how to improve myself. This is the highest self-cultivation. The last sentence is: what is said must be done, and knowledge and action must be united.
